<div id="review_224902671" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224902671" />
    <a title="Ann Collette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5817942-ann-collette"><img alt="Ann Collette" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224902671?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann Collette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann Collette" href="/user/show/5817942-ann-collette">Ann Collette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224902671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18346068943712756869">There's been a lot of noise lately about Amazon bypassing major commercial publishers and publishing books directly themselves. Based on this deadly dull "thriller," major commercial publishing has nothing to worry about. I have no idea why it's called THE HANGMAN'S DAUGHTER, cause she doesn't play much of a role in the book. I have no idea why the translator of this book was chosen for the job, since he not only has zero understanding of pace but has no feel at all for the time period the book </span>
  <span id="freeText18346068943712756869" style="display:none">There's been a lot of noise lately about Amazon bypassing major commercial publishers and publishing books directly themselves. Based on this deadly dull "thriller," major commercial publishing has nothing to worry about. I have no idea why it's called THE HANGMAN'S DAUGHTER, cause she doesn't play much of a role in the book. I have no idea why the translator of this book was chosen for the job, since he not only has zero understanding of pace but has no feel at all for the time period the book is set in -- 1659. Um, did they have "grammar schools" then? Or wear "trousers?" Or, my favorite -- "if we don't have the true culprit by then, they won't screw around for long..." Man, can't you just HEAR the folks of 1659 and how they talked in that sentence! <br />The book is about a hangman taking it upon himself to investigate the murders of some orphans in his Bavarian town. He's a wise giant of a man, somewhat troubled by the nature of his job (which also includes torturing suspects in order to get a confession out of them) joined in his search for the murderer by a young physician just starting to question the old ways. Pages and pages of tedious description slow this book down to a halt repeatedly. Nothing about it ever came alive for me. I don't know how much is the author's fault or the translator's fault and I don't care -- both are men of limited talent. The author doesn't even address one of the the biggest stumbling blocks he sets up in the book regarding the desired marriage between the foppish young doctor and the hangman's daughter (laws of the time prevented members of a hangman's family from marrying anyone other than a member of another hangman's family), ending the book without ever resolving it. But it's not like I really cared -- about this, or anyone or anything in this jaw-popping bore of a novel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18346068943712756869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer123879521651712048">Well, this was a new experience for me! I downloaded the Kindle version for free during a promotion, and discovered that it was not only illustrated, but ANIMATED! I've never seen such a thing, but it was so cool! Torches would light, the map of the town would become more detailed, the hangman's ragged coat would blow in the wind! Crazy stuff! Honestly, if not that for that, this would have been a four star book. It's fascinating, it was full of action and mystery and horrifying torture, but . .</span>
  <span id="freeText123879521651712048" style="display:none">Well, this was a new experience for me! I downloaded the Kindle version for free during a promotion, and discovered that it was not only illustrated, but ANIMATED! I've never seen such a thing, but it was so cool! Torches would light, the map of the town would become more detailed, the hangman's ragged coat would blow in the wind! Crazy stuff! Honestly, if not that for that, this would have been a four star book. It's fascinating, it was full of action and mystery and horrifying torture, but . . . I kind of wasn't sure who I was rooting for? The hangman was my favorite, but he still had to do his job and torture the poor midwife! She wasn't helping her own case at all, either! And I really kind of wanted the entire town council to be murdered, because I hated each one of them, except that one guy, who was actually nice, but other than him . . . what a bunch of assholes! <br /><br />If you do read this (and if you like historical mysteries, you will love this), READ THE KINDLE EDITION. It's so cool!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_442762075" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/442762075" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/442762075?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=ebook_kindle">ebook_kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=made-my-eyes-bleed">made-my-eyes-bleed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer442762075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5483488870606223078"><i>"Germany, 1660: When a dying boy is pulled from the river with a mark crudely tattooed on his shoulder, hangman Jakob Kuisl is called upon to investigate whether witchcraft is at play. So begins The Hangman's Daughter--the chillingly detailed, fast-paced historical thriller[...]"</i><br/><br/>I think it was set in Germany, somewhere around 1660 (who's counting?), but otherwise, the description for this book is full of lies. The mark wasn't "tattooed" crudely or otherwise, it was drawn in freaking berry juice.</span>
  <span id="freeText5483488870606223078" style="display:none"><i>"Germany, 1660: When a dying boy is pulled from the river with a mark crudely tattooed on his shoulder, hangman Jakob Kuisl is called upon to investigate whether witchcraft is at play. So begins The Hangman's Daughter--the chillingly detailed, fast-paced historical thriller[...]"</i><br /><br />I think it was set in Germany, somewhere around 1660 (who's counting?), but otherwise, the description for this book is full of lies. The mark wasn't "tattooed" crudely or otherwise, it was drawn in freaking berry juice. Sure, it's a mark on the skin, but a tattoo is NOT just any mark on the skin. That's like saying that Kool-aid mustaches are tattoos. Dramatic much? <br /><br />Next, Jakob Kuisl wasn't "called upon" to investigate anything. He was told to torture a confession out of a woman, whether she was guilty or not, because it was the most expedient resolution. He took it upon himself to investigate, and was repeatedly told to STOP investigating by the town authorities. <br /><br />Then, the title. The Hangman's Daughter. Why is that the title? What does she have to do with the story at all? Nothing. The answer is nothing. She was a character in it, sure, but not an important one, and if she'd been removed from the story, it would have been just as boring, but wouldn't have suffered any other way. She added nothing to the story. She didn't help figure out the mystery. She didn't progress the plot. She was there as a "star-crossed" love interest to one of the main characters, and as a convenient way to piss off daddy. The title was probably just chosen because being someone's daughter in book titles was all the rage a few years back and it was a way to fit in with what all the other cool books were doing. <br /><br />Finally, this "the chillingly detailed, fast-paced historical thriller" was anything but. I have never been so bored by innumerable descriptions of torture methods and witch hunts. Everything was repeated over and over and over again. The same thing, sometimes two or three times in a row, just different ways, as though the reader just couldn't quite get the point the first time. Filler, filler, filler. <br /><br />I'm annoyed because I'd heard many great things about this series, and I'd actually bought the second and third books in the series when I saw them at a booksale... and now they will be going right back out in the donation pile, because getting through one book was tedious enough. I'm not going to put myself through that two more times. <br /><br />I can't really think of anything that I liked about this book. The characters were all super flat, the dialogue was stilted and cliche, the writing was awkward (though in fairness, that could be due to the fact that it's a translation), and the plot was sooooooooo boring. <br /><br />Yup, that about sums it up. That's all I got. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5483488870606223078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2791045896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2791045896" />
    <a title="Elizabeth (Alaska)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2026178-elizabeth-alaska"><img alt="Elizabeth (Alaska)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304966095p2/2026178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2791045896?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth (Alaska)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth (Alaska)" href="/user/show/2026178-elizabeth-alaska">Elizabeth (Alaska)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/37808197-the-hangman-s-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=europe-other">europe-other</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=twenty-first-century">twenty-first-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2026178-elizabeth-alaska?shelf=potzsch">potzsch</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2791045896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer828765191392820547">Jakob Kuisl is the Hangman of the title. The term hangman sort of lumps together his all around function of the town, for hanging is not the only form of execution. Further, he is the one who tortures in order to extract confessions. He is a huge man and well suited to the profession that has been handed down from father to son for generations. But Kuisl finds it against his very nature to conduct the actions required and when he knows an execution or interrogation is on the horizon he chooses t</span>
  <span id="freeText828765191392820547" style="display:none">Jakob Kuisl is the Hangman of the title. The term hangman sort of lumps together his all around function of the town, for hanging is not the only form of execution. Further, he is the one who tortures in order to extract confessions. He is a huge man and well suited to the profession that has been handed down from father to son for generations. But Kuisl finds it against his very nature to conduct the actions required and when he knows an execution or interrogation is on the horizon he chooses to get blind drunk. Not to avoid doing the job, but just to get himself through a job that he is both well suited for and hates with a passion. <br /><br />Call me perverse, but PÃ¶tzsch drops a bit of humor into this black-sounding drama. One of my GR friends (thank you, Emma) says "I would class the genre of the book as a romance/historical fiction/detective fiction hybrid." Certainly the novel contains all three elements, though I might put the romance element third. It, too, provides humor. The daughter of the title is flirtatious and a bit of a siren who has eyes only for the physician Simon Fronwieser. Fronwieser, who is a bit of a dandy, also provides a bit of humor. <br /><br />This is not a novel with beautiful prose which would probably be inappropriate. The writing style is interesting, though I did note a bit of repetition here and there. Most of the characterizations are two-dimensional with the exception of Jakob Kuisl. I'll leave it to others to say that it is historically accurate. This is not a period with which I am familiar, and, frankly, am glad the world has left behind the belief in witchcraft and has gained medical knowledge. <br /><br />I picked this up when Amazon Crossing had some free offerings earlier this year. They followed up with inexpensively priced issues of the remaining installments of the series. I can't say why I felt disposed to purchase them all, but I'm glad I did. It is not 5-star material - as much because of the mystery/romance element as anything. I found myself looking forward to my time with it and am happy to give it a solid 4-stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="828765191392820547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1945311737" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1945311737" />
    <a title="Johanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58260626-johanna"><img alt="Johanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473771266p2/58260626.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1945311737?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johanna" href="/user/show/58260626-johanna">Johanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783548268521" href="/book/show/6100123-die-henkerstochter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58260626-johanna?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58260626-johanna?shelf=crime-thriller">crime-thriller</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1945311737" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11759380459528912349">I've been reading too much fantasy lately and needed a break â¦ so I decided to read a historical crime fiction involving witches â¦ yeah â¦ in my head that made a lot more sense.<br/>First let me mention a little complaint here. Despite being titled The Hangman's Daughter â¦ this book isn't actually about the hangman's daughter. Of the 500 pages and multiple POV's maybe 50 were from Magdalena's POV (the titular hangman's daughter), which is only slightly more than the wrongfully accused midwife. The act</span>
  <span id="freeText11759380459528912349" style="display:none">I've been reading too much fantasy lately and needed a break â¦ so I decided to read a historical crime fiction involving witches â¦ yeah â¦ in my head that made a lot more sense.<br />First let me mention a little complaint here. Despite being titled The Hangman's Daughter â¦ this book isn't actually about the hangman's daughter. Of the 500 pages and multiple POV's maybe 50 were from Magdalena's POV (the titular hangman's daughter), which is only slightly more than the wrongfully accused midwife. The actual main characters are Magdalena's father (the hangman), Jacob, and the son of the local medicus, Simon (who also happens to have a crush on Magdalena and vice versa).<br />Prepare to be disturbed!!! Jacob's memories of the past and the details of his occupation are very brutal. Over all this book really isn't for the weak of mind â¦ or stomach. There are details of executions, war memories, and torture scenes which are all the more horrifying because they are historically accurate.<br />Choosing the hangman as one of the main POVs and have him be a likeable character is quite unique and very interesting. The dynamic between Jacob and Simon was intriguing as well, especially in the way it defied social conventions of the time.<br />The plot was a good mixture of politics, prejudice, fear, and social issues. Though I'm not sure just how much people who have no knowledge of German history will pick up of the last. All in all I enjoyed the book and will likely continue the series once the books are available at my local library.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11759380459528912349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14199629703477039808">This was definitely a page turner. I couldn't put the book down at times. The ending moved a little slow. This was the story about the executioner Jakob Kuisl and his mission to save the midwife Martha from a crime that she did not commit. Children were dying and on their backs were a witchâs symbol. They blamed the midwife for being a witch and had her arrested and tortured until she admitted that she committed the crime. Jakob knew that the midwife was innocent. Two children were murdered afte</span>
  <span id="freeText14199629703477039808" style="display:none">This was definitely a page turner. I couldn't put the book down at times. The ending moved a little slow. This was the story about the executioner Jakob Kuisl and his mission to save the midwife Martha from a crime that she did not commit. Children were dying and on their backs were a witchâs symbol. They blamed the midwife for being a witch and had her arrested and tortured until she admitted that she committed the crime. Jakob knew that the midwife was innocent. Two children were murdered after she was arrested. The people say she summoned the devil for help because he was seen leaving one of the orphanâs house. He and Simon the local physicianâs son set out to prove her innocence. The crime started out with just the ruining of the lepers house they were building and a group of orphans overheard the deal and they were dealt a death sentence. Three children dead, a burnt up warehouse, and a destroyed leper house had Jakob and Simon on the run trying to solve the mystery. Simon is in love with the executionerâs daughter Magdalena. However, this love can never be because being the executionerâs daughter is a lowly position and she must marry another executionerâs son. She chimes in and helps the other two solve this mystery and ends up getting kidnapped herself. This puts Jakob against the devil himself. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14199629703477039808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('otJcKbGMm5ayUeDKM8rSgbsH0CznyeMRpRBo9EOJk4pXZe5c8zjGNFGx96FYQlKjMuVPIOxi0h21BtHcCk5oOQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer14458025366265976689">Oliver PÃ¶tzsch is a German writer and filmmaker. After high school he attended the German School of Journalism in Munich from 1992 to 1997. He then worked for Radio Bavaria. In addition to his professional activities in radio and television, PÃ¶tzsch researched his family history.
